{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01JA2VuwKyGHrPacM8DYTKFa","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2023 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package wait\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"math\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"time\\\"\\n24: \\n25: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\\\"\\n26: \\t\\\"k8s.io/utils/clock\\\"\\n27: )\\n28: \\n29: // Backoff holds parameters applied to a Backoff function.\\n30: type Backoff struct {\\n31: \\t// The initial duration.\\n32: \\tDuration time.Duration\\n33: \\t// Duration is multiplied by factor each iteration, if factor is not zero\\n34: \\t// and the limits imposed by Steps and Cap have not been reached.\\n35: \\t// Should not be negative.\\n36: \\t// The jitter does not contribute to the updates to the duration parameter.\\n37: \\tFactor float64\\n38: \\t// The sleep at each iteration is the duration plus an additional\\n39: \\t// amount chosen uniformly at random from the interval between\\n40: \\t// zero and `jitter*duration`.\\n41: \\tJitter float64\\n42: \\t// The remaining number of iterations in which the duration\\n43: \\t// parameter may change (but progress can be stopped earlier by\\n44: \\t// hitting the cap). If not positive, the duration is not\\n45: \\t// changed. Used for exponential backoff in combination with\\n46: \\t// Factor and Cap.\\n47: \\tSteps int\\n48: \\t// A limit on revised values of the duration parameter. If a\\n49: \\t// multiplication by the factor parameter would make the duration\\n50: \\t// exceed the cap then the duration is set to the cap and the\\n51: \\t// steps parameter is set to zero.\\n52: \\tCap time.Duration\\n53: }\\n54: \\n55: // Step returns an amount of time to sleep determined by the original\\n56: // Duration and Jitter. The backoff is mutated to update its Steps and\\n57: // Duration. A nil Backoff always has a zero-duration step.\\n58: func (b *Backoff) Step() time.Duration {\\n59: \\tif b == nil {\\n60: \\t\\treturn 0\\n61: \\t}\\n62: \\tvar nextDuration time.Duration\\n63: \\tnextDuration, b.Duration, b.Steps = delay(b.Steps, b.Duration, b.Cap, b.Factor, b.Jitter)\\n64: \\treturn nextDuration\\n65: }\\n66: \\n67: // DelayFunc returns a function that will compute the next interval to\\n68: // wait given the arguments in b. \"Exponential backoff retry implementations across three major Go projects demonstrate consistent patterns for handling transient failures.\\n\\nIn Kubernetes (kubernetes/kubernetes), exponential backoff is implemented in multiple layers: The core infrastructure in staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait/backoff.go provides the Backoff struct and ExponentialBackoff/ExponentialBackoffWithContext functions that implement the exponential backoff algorithm using a delay function with configurable Duration, Factor, Jitter, Steps, and Cap. The pkg/util/goroutinemap/exponentialbackoff/exponential_backoff.go module provides a specialized ExponentialBackoff type for goroutine operations that tracks lastError, lastErrorTime, and durationBeforeRetry, doubling the wait duration on each failure until reaching maxDurationBeforeRetry (2 minutes 2 seconds). This pattern is used throughout the kubelet (volumemanager/reconciler, pluginmanager/reconciler) and volume attachment/detachment reconcilers. The staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/webhook/webhook.go implements WithExponentialBackoff for webhook retry logic.\\n\\nIn Grafana (grafana/grafana), exponential backoff appears in three distinct implementations: The apps/provisioning/pkg/repository/git/repository.go uses retry.ExponentialBackoffRetrier (imported from the external nanogit library) via the defaultGitRetrier function, configured with 8 total attempts (1 initial + 7 retries), 100ms initial delay, 5 second max delay, 2.0 multiplier, and jitter. The pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/retry.go implements a custom exponentialBackoffRetryer struct wrapping the backoff.BackOff interface, used for alert rule and recording rule evaluation with configurable max retries, initial/max delays, and clock support. The pkg/util/retryer/retryer.go provides a generic Retry function that uses exponential backoff starting from minDelay and increasing to maxDelay after each failure.\\n\\nIn Prometheus (prometheus/prometheus), exponential backoff is central to remote write resilience: The storage/remote/queue_manager.go implements sendWriteRequestWithBackoff that manages retry logic for write requests, starting with the minimum configured backoff and respecting Retry-After headers from remote endpoints. The config/config.go defines QueueConfig with MinBackoff (default 30ms) and MaxBackoff (default 5 seconds) fields that control the exponential backoff behavior during write failures. This pattern is used throughout the kubelet (volumemanager/reconciler, pluginmanager/reconciler) and volume attachment/detachment reconcilers.
